Animatory state tiles

Click a tile in the gallery below to see the following info:

0x00: row 1, column 1
lsb=0x82, ref_page=0xDD
ref_addr=(lsb,ref_page)=DD82
ref=0x03, udg_page=0xC7
udg_addr=(ref,udg_page)=C703

where:

  • lsb is the animatory state + 0x80 + n (n=2 if the animatory state is divisible by 8, n=0 otherwise)
  • ref_page is the page containing the UDG reference for the tile (0xD7-0xE5)
  • ref_addr is the address of the UDG reference (lsb+0100*ref_page)
  • ref is the UDG reference at ref_addr (0x00-0xD6, 0xD9-0xFF)
  • udg_page is the base page for the tile graphic data (always 0xC7)
  • udg_addr is the base address of the tile graphic data (ref+0100*udg_page)

The graphic for an animatory state is made up of 4 or 15 tiles in a 2x2, 3x5 or 5x3, grid:

02
13
0510
1611
2712
3813
4914
036912
1471013
2581114

Each tile has a UDG reference (ref) located at (lsb,T+0xD7), where T is the tile number (0-14).

The eight graphic bytes and eight mask bytes for a tile are located thus:

AddressContents
(ref,udg_page)=udg_addr Graphic byte 1/8
(ref,udg_page+0x01)=udg_addr+0100 Mask byte 1/8
(ref,udg_page+0x02)=udg_addr+0200 Graphic byte 2/8
(ref,udg_page+0x03)=udg_addr+0300 Mask byte 2/8
(ref,udg_page+0x04)=udg_addr+0400 Graphic byte 3/8
(ref,udg_page+0x05)=udg_addr+0500 Mask byte 3/8
(ref,udg_page+0x06)=udg_addr+0600 Graphic byte 4/8
(ref,udg_page+0x07)=udg_addr+0700 Mask byte 4/8
(ref,udg_page+0x08)=udg_addr+0800 Graphic byte 5/8
(ref,udg_page+0x09)=udg_addr+0900 Mask byte 5/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0A)=udg_addr+0A00 Graphic byte 6/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0B)=udg_addr+0B00 Mask byte 6/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0C)=udg_addr+0C00 Graphic byte 7/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0D)=udg_addr+0D00 Mask byte 7/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0E)=udg_addr+0E00 Graphic byte 8/8
(ref,udg_page+0x0F)=udg_addr+0F00 Mask byte 8/8

The 'null' UDG (ref=0x00) is always taken to be blank (eight zeroes); its graphic data is not looked up at (0x00,0xC7).

Any given tile (identified by udg_addr) may appear in more than one animatory state (and in more than one place in a single animatory state).

The tiles for animatory states 0x80-0xFF are not stored separately; the tiles for animatory state N>=0x80 are obtained by flipping the tiles for animatory state N-0x80 (see E8F3).
